Sino-French Through Air Service, Test Flight Preparations Imminent 114

Nie Kaiyi of China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) in Charge

China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC), responsible for handling the Sino-French through air service, immediately assigned its air navigation group to prepare for test flights after receiving instructions from the Ministry of Communications. It is reported that CNAC Director Pissis had previously completed the route survey from Guangzhou to Saigon and Hanoi, so the test flight may still fly this route first. The French side is reported to be flying from Marseille through French territory to Saigon, while the Chinese side will fly from Guangzhou through various districts of the Guangzhou Bay and South Road to Saigon and Hanoi, with Hanoi as the interchange point. If the weather clears, the test flight may depart from Guangzhou after the New Year holiday next year. The head of the Air Navigation Group, Nie Kaiyi, will personally oversee the operation at that time.

Key Points of the Third Phase of the "Three-izations" Lifestyle 115

To Be Implemented from New Year's Day

The Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association began to implement the "militarization, industrialization, and artification" plan for lifestyle this year, starting with civil servants in various government agencies, issuing key points in phases, from the simple to the complex, step by step. The first phase of key points has already been fully implemented and the results have been tallied and published. The second phase will also be fully implemented by the end of this month, pending assessment. Therefore, the third phase of key points will be implemented from January 1st next year. The Association has already issued a copy to each agency and official in the city, and the responsible leaders are responsible for supervising and urging compliance. The content of these key points is aimed at correcting bad habits and reversing the decline, so if everyone can put them into practice, it will benefit both public and private interests, and the social atmosphere will be greatly changed. The original text of the third phase of key points is recorded below: "Preliminary Plan for the Implementation of the Three-izations Lifestyle in Shanghai Agencies", Third Phase Key Points (To be implemented from January 1, 1936)

Principles

To cultivate swift and orderly action; to cultivate a life of labor and frugality; to cultivate habits of politeness and law-abiding. (A) Pertaining to Militarization: Hair should not be too long, should not be oiled, and should not be permed; in the office, be energetic in work, do not joke around, do not make noise, do not doze off; stipulate personal work and rest times, read useful books and newspapers in your spare time. (B) Pertaining to Industrialization: Vigorously practice frugality, tighten various public and private consumptions; do not borrow money from others unless absolutely necessary, and must return it immediately after borrowing, do not break your promise; live within your means, record all income and expenditure items one by one. (C) Pertaining to Artification: Do not easily quarrel, should be calm and peaceful; be helpful to others, do not only consider your own interests; do not flatter others, do not insult others, should respect your own and others' personality.

Explanation

These key points are based on the implementation plan issued by the General Association, taking into account the actual situation in Shanghai. They are from the simple to the complex, implemented in phases. Civil servants in various agencies are role models for citizens, so they must first regard the three-izations lifestyle as a standard of conduct and strive to implement it. The heads of each agency are responsible for supervising and promoting the full responsibility of implementing these key points. When implementing these key points, the third phase of key points must continue to be diligently implemented without slackening. These key points are for a period of two months, and the New Life Movement Association may inspect them at any time during implementation.

Land Bureau: Measures for Clearing Overflow Land, Increasing Taxes, etc. 119

The Shanghai Land Bureau's clearance of backlog cases and extension of office hours was reported in previous news. It is now learned that the Bureau has formulated measures for clearing the unsettled cases of overflow land and tax increases, as well as for clearing the cases of land with license and land applied for along the streets which have been completed but the prices have not been paid, and has submitted them to the Municipal Government for approval and promulgated them to the people of the city for general knowledge so that they can comply with the payment and issuance of certificates. The announcement and measures are explored and recorded below.

Public Announcement

It is hereby announced that since the Land Bureau conducted a survey of land in this city, many cases of overflow land have been discovered, which should be subject to tax increases and price payments according to regulations. It is currently estimated that after the Bureau notified the owners of this overflow land, there are still about 1,200 cases who have not come to the Bureau to pay the price. In addition, there are more than 100 cases of tax increases for land with permits and land applied for along the streets, which the Bureau has notified but have not yet been paid. These are all payments that the owners should make, but they have repeatedly delayed, resulting in long-standing arrears, making it difficult to clear and issue documents, and affecting the city's revenue. Among them, many owners have been waiting and seeing, and it is inevitable that some are unable to pay. Now, in order to show consideration for the owners and facilitate their raising of funds for payment, those who pay in full within three months will be given a discount on the originally determined amount to be paid. Once cleared, certificates will be issued within two weeks to show consideration. If they are really unable to pay the price in one lump sum, they will be allowed to pay in installments over the years, and interest will be charged appropriately to show fairness. The measures for clearing the unsettled cases of overflow land and tax increases, as well as the measures for clearing the cases of land with permits and land applied for along the streets which have been completed but the prices have not been paid, have been separately drafted and submitted to the Municipal Government for approval. The two types of measures mentioned above are hereby announced to the people of the city so that all landowners regarding cases where overflow land has been measured, as well as tax increases for land with permits and land applied for along the streets, which have been notified by the Bureau before October 18, 1935, must comply with the measures below and come to the Bureau to pay and obtain certificates, and do not err again. This is specially announced. December 28, 1935, Cai Zengji, concurrently acting Land Bureau Director. Attachment:

Clearance Measures

(A) Measures for Clearing the Unsettled Cases of Overflow Land and Tax Increases: All owners of overflow land and tax increases who pay the full amount within one month after this announcement and notification will have the originally determined amount reduced to 70 percent. Within two months, it will be reduced to 75 percent. Within three months, it will be reduced to 80 percent. After three months, the original amount to be paid will still be paid, and interest will be added from the date of the announcement. In the special zone, the monthly interest rate is 8 percent. In the urban commercial district, the monthly interest rate is 6 percent. In the non-urban commercial district, the monthly interest rate is 4 percent. If it is less than one month, it will be counted as one month. If half of the amount is paid first within three months after the announcement and notification, the remaining half will be allowed to be paid in installments over the years. The half paid first will be reduced to 75 percent within one month after the announcement, 80 percent within two months, and 85 percent within three months. The half to be paid in installments will still be calculated at the original amount in full. In the special zone, it will be allowed to be paid in three equal annual installments. In the urban commercial district, it will be allowed to be paid in five years. In the non-urban commercial district, it will be allowed to be paid in eight years, all without interest. If there is a transfer of ownership during the installment period, the full amount should be paid at once. Whether the full amount is paid in one lump sum or in installments, the business license will be issued within two weeks after the full amount is verified and collected. During the installment period, the full amount can be paid at any time to obtain the certificate. If there are buildings rented out or people renting land for construction on land containing overflow land, a minimum of installment payment according to Article 2 must be made within three months. If this is not complied with, effective measures will be taken to deal with it. These clearance measures will be promulgated and implemented after being submitted to the Municipal Government for approval. (B) Measures for Clearing the Cases of Land with Permits and Land Applied for Along the Streets which have been Completed but the Prices have not been Paid: All owners of land with permits and land applied for along the streets who have not yet complied with the notification to pay the price will be handled in accordance with the following provisions after this announcement and notification: A. Those who pay the full amount within one month will have it reduced to 80 percent (calculated according to the amount payable in the first notification, the same below). B. Those who pay in full within two months will have it reduced to 85 percent. C. Those who pay half the amount within one month and pay the full amount within two months will have the first half reduced to 80 percent and the second half reduced to 85 percent. Those who pay in full within three months will have the second half reduced to 90 percent. Those who pay in full within four months will have the second half reduced to 95 percent. D. Those who pay half the amount within two months will have the first half reduced to 85 percent and the second half reduced to 90 percent. Those who pay in full within four months will have half the amount reduced to 95 percent. Land with permits in the four districts of the French Concession, including Gaohang, Luhang, Yangjingtang, and Qiaotang, where the full price is paid, will be further reduced by 10 percent based on the previously determined reduction rates. Those who pay the full amount in one lump sum will be issued a business certificate two weeks later. Those who pay the full amount in two installments will be issued a certificate within three days after the second installment is completed. If the price is not paid within two months or the first half of the price is paid and the second installment is overdue, it should be deemed as a waiver of rights, and the case will be canceled and dealt with according to the following regulations: A. The land with a permit will be released for application separately. After the release, the original price of the permit will be refunded. B. The land along the streets will be released separately. In all of the above cases, if the first installment has been paid, it will not be refunded.

County Government Levies the Second Installment of Land Tax 120

The Shanghai County Government began levying the first installment of the land tax for 1935 on September 1, which has already expired. Therefore, it has continued to levy the second installment yesterday and has complied with the order to set the deadline as January 23, 1936. The autumn survey of this year was submitted to the Department of Finance for approval, and it was generally reduced by 10 percent. The second installment of the land tax license will deduct the corresponding amount to actually levy five-sixths. In addition to distributing the notification forms to various Bao-Tu treasuries for distribution, it also announces to the owners for general compliance and payment at the treasury on schedule to draw the certificate and settle the industry.

Post Office Bureau: Improving Parcel Delivery from New Year's Day 121

Waiver of Parcel Inspection Procedures at Various Ports Along the Yangtze River

In order to facilitate the public, the Ministry of Communications' Directorate General of Posts is improving parcel delivery, and the Shanghai Post Office Bureau has been ordered to implement it from New Year's Day next year. The details are explored below.

Improving Delivery

Since the Directorate General of Posts moved to Nanjing, it has been working harder to promote postal affairs. In areas where inland rail is not accessible, the original regulations stipulated 20 kilograms for parcels. In order to facilitate the public, the Bureau will change it to 30 kilograms from New Year's Day next year. However, those forwarded through foreign post will still be limited to 20 kilograms. The Bureau in this port has decided to implement it as scheduled. In addition, the Directorate General is actively planning for general postal awards and postal services in border areas.

Waiver of Parcel Inspection

After the Customs implemented the abolition of parcel transit tax last November, the Directorate General of Posts and the Inspector General of Customs negotiated this autumn to reduce and exempt parcel inspection procedures to facilitate postal delivery. The Directorate General of Posts has now ordered post offices in various places that, in addition to parcels received and sent by post offices at border and coastal trading ports, which may be randomly inspected by the Customs at any time, parcel inspections will be reduced and exempted at ports along the Yangtze River from now on, including Zhenjiang, Nanjing, Wuhu, Jiujiang, Hankou, Yueyang, Changsha, Shashi, Yichang, Wanxian, Chongqing, and other eleven places.

Through Train between Shanghai and Peiping Cancels Stopping Time at Langfang Station 122

Effective January 1, 1936

According to the Bureau of Railways, in order to increase the speed of the through trains No. 301 and No. 302 between Shanghai and Peiping on the Beijing-Shenyang Railway, it has been approved to cancel the stopping time of the two trains at Langfang Station and stop selling tickets from January 1 next year. Passengers transferring to that station should take other appropriate trains.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Writes to Central Bank Requesting Jiangwan Post Office to Exchange Legal Tender 124

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce wrote to the Central Bank yesterday, stating: We are writing to you because we have investigated the eight articles of the measures for unifying the exchange of legal tender in the Ministry of Finance's November telegram. Article 2 states that post offices entrusted by the designated banks may also serve as legal tender exchange agencies. There are no banks established in the Jiangwan district of this city, only the post office, but the post office refuses to accept exchanges because it has no orders from above, causing great inconvenience to merchants and the public. We hereby request that your bank consult with the Post Office Bureau to entrust the post offices in the towns and villages of this city where no bank branches are established to handle the exchange of legal tender so as to meet the fundamental purpose of facilitating the people. According to the report from the branch office of this association, the Jiangwan district is particularly in need, and we would like to ask for your immediate transfer to facilitate implementation.

Grain Merchants Telegraph Southwest Authorities Again Urging the Abolition of Bran Surtax 125

Unclogging Accumulated Goods to Relieve Merchant Hardship

The Shanghai Grain, Oil Cake, and other trade groups telegraphed the Southwest authorities again yesterday to appeal for the abolition of the bran surtax. The original telegram reads: Distributed to Principal Zou of Zhongshan University, Chairman Lin of the Southwest Political Affairs Committee and the Guangdong Provincial Government, and the Commissioner's Office of Guangdong Finance: We have been requesting the abolition of the Guangdong Province's surcharge on domestic bran for the Zhongshan University construction fund for four months. Manufacturers and transporters from various places have repeatedly appealed, and during the Fifth National Congress, they jointly petitioned in Nanjing. The reply was that factories should resume work first, and the case would be submitted to the competent authorities of the National Government for correction, etc. At the same time, we met with Your Excellency (Principal Zou of Zhongshan University), who agreed to return to Guangdong to resolve the matter. Oil factories from various places resumed work on the 25th of last month, but more than a month has passed since then. The goods have accumulated, silver stocks are blocked, and we are struggling to maintain ourselves in great pain. Furthermore, it has been found that the First Plenary Session of the Central Committee passed a resolution on the Zhongshan University construction fund at the beginning of this month, indicating that the government has already raised funds separately for the Zhongshan University construction fund. There is no factual difficulty in abolishing the Guangdong Province's surcharge on domestic bran. It is learned that Your Excellency (Principal Zou) has already returned to Guangdong and will be able to abolish it immediately. In order to resolve the pain as soon as possible, the merchants have no choice but to telegraph again, appealing to Your Excellency (Committee) (Office) to approve the Merchants Political Committee to maintain the order of May last year that only soybean bran from the three northeastern provinces should not be subject to tax, and to issue a clear order to exempt or levy taxes on bran from the Northeast and domestic production before the end of December this year, so as to unclog the accumulated goods as soon as possible and relieve merchant hardship. The representatives of the Shanghai Grain, Oil Cake, Oil Press, Guangdong Native Grain, and Chaozhou Sugar and Grocery Trade Associations, Gu Xinyi, respectfully.

Jinda University Professor Zhou Xianwen Discusses Currency Issues 128

China Should Persist in Its New Monetary Policy

A Central News Agency reporter interviewed Zhou Xianwen, director of the Department of Business Administration at Jinda University, yesterday and discussed China's monetary issues. Zhou Min made the following comments (below are Mr. Zhou's words): According to the new monetary system promulgated in China on November 4, it was originally beneficial to the ups and downs of silver prices (the reverse being the fall in the value of our currency). In a sense, it can also be said to be the result of the United States implementing its silver purchase policy, which caused silver prices to continue to rise. Therefore, scholars have advocated taking the opportunity to sell silver and buy gold, and to adopt a de facto gold standard. However, it was not long before it was rumored that the United States' silver purchase policy would change, and London silver prices fell sharply. Now, taking Shanghai's gold standard as an example, since the currency reform, gold prices have been stable between 1,140 and 1,150 yuan, but now they have lost their normal state and have risen sharply (the reverse being the fall in silver prices), once reaching 1,200 yuan. Therefore, the idea of increasing customs duties and reducing foreign exchange has been widely spread in the market, and some scholars have once again advocated adopting a silver bullion standard. To say that a country's monetary system, which is of utmost importance to the national economy, can change with the rising and falling silver prices overseas, and can be either gold or silver, changing as frequently as morning and evening, is somewhat ridiculous. In my opinion, the difficulty China faces today is that it is caught in the crossfire of the economic policies of various countries and cannot be independent. If it leans to A, it will be damaged by B; if it leans to B, it will be attacked by C. Therefore, if our monetary system is to be truly effective, it must be based on the true liberation of the nation and the true independence of the country. As for the means of treating the symptoms, we must persist in the original intent of the authorities when issuing the currency system and gradually improve it based on the new facts. (Central News Agency)

Case of Detectives Obstructing Freedom; Police Response in Official Letter 133

Judge Orders Further Interrogation After Negotiation. Fan Tingzhang, a Ningbo native and owner of Lao Song Mao South Goods Store at the intersection of Ward Road and Jingzhou Road in the Public Concession, and Fan Wenzhao, his cousin and owner of Da Lai Printing Ink Factory at No. 12 Chong Rang Li, Fuzhou Road, previously, along with lawyer Sun Zuji, filed a complaint with the Criminal Court of the Special Second Court, accusing Wang Dongming, a Tianjin native and detective of the French Police, of privately handcuffing them, obstructing their freedom, and publicly insulting them, requesting the court to order the defendant to appear in court and be investigated according to law. Wang Wangxu, the president of the (Special First) Court, opened a court session on the 21st of this month, first summoning the plaintiffs to appear and inquire. Fan Wenzhao was unable to arrive in time due to business in Hankou, and only Fan Tingzhang, accompanied by his agent, lawyer Sun, appeared in court. The judge ordered a postponement for further trial. This has been reported in detail in this newspaper. At 2:00 PM yesterday, Judge Wang again summoned the parties in the Second Criminal Court. The defendant, Wang Dongming, did not appear. The plaintiffs, Fan Tingzhang and Fan Wenzhao, arrived with their lawyer. According to Fan Wenzhao's testimony, it was the same as Fan Tingzhang's previous testimony. The judge said to the two plaintiffs, "After this court sent the summons to the defendant, the police sent an official letter stating that you were indeed impersonating detectives at the time. Did you actually impersonate detectives?" The Fans replied in unison, "We went to mediate a dispute between my sister and her tenant. There was absolutely no impersonation of detectives." The plaintiff's lawyer explained to the court, "If the police believed that the two plaintiffs were impersonating detectives at the time, then why did the police not immediately prosecute them? Now, the police say that the plaintiffs impersonated detectives, which is not plausible." After reviewing the statements, the court ordered a postponement for further trial after negotiation, and the judge adjourned the court.

Uncle Murders Sister-in-Law 134

Qiu Heng's Poisoning Plot Foiled

Escaped While on Bail, Father Arrested

Qiu Hengzhong, a native of Hubei (34 years old), was a Western doctor and had a long-standing improper relationship with his widowed sister-in-law, Huiying. Last September, due to differing opinions, Huiying came to Shanghai in anger and rented a house in Xinxian Li, Hugunying, Nanshi. Qiu Hengzhong found out about this and followed her to Shanghai, staying at the home of his friend Li Xiyan (who worked as a court clerk in the Special First Court). He then found out Huiying's address and, together with Li Xiyan, invited Huiying to talk at the Yangzi Hotel, generously giving her travel expenses and asking her to leave Shanghai. Qiu and Huiying left together and took a Lilli taxi pre-hired by Li Xiyan to the Shanghai-Minhang South Zhe Road. Qiu Hengzhong suddenly became murderous, taking out cotton soaked in hydrochloric acid, morphine, and other poisons, which he had hidden on his person, intending to stuff it into his sister-in-law's mouth to harm her. Huiying saw this and struggled desperately, jumping out of the car. The taxi driver, seeing this, stopped the car in a panic and ran to inform the police, who arrested Qiu Hengzhong and brought him to the District Court Prosecutor's Office. After questioning, he was released on bail pending trial. Prosecutor Ouyang Shu's investigation was clear, and he was prosecuted for attempted murder. Judge He Jingcen repeatedly summoned him for questioning, but after Qiu Hengzhong was released on bail, he fled to Wuchang and remained at large. Later, the court found out where Qiu was hiding and sent police to Wuchang to bring Qiu back to Shanghai and detain him. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Judge He opened court again. The plaintiff, Qiu Huiyang, did not appear. After the judge took his seat, he ordered the detained Qiu Hengzhong to be brought to the dock. Qiu claimed, "I had arguments with my sister-in-law due to verbal conflicts and differing opinions, but the two bottles of medicine and cotton were not mine. It is a false accusation that I tried to harm her. Please investigate." After hearing the statement, the judge believed the case was clear and began the debate, which was concluded. The court would render a judgment at a later date, and the defendant was returned to custody.

Two Customers Drink Free of Charge 135

Fake Handgun Discovered, Landlord and Landlady Come to Assist

Both Men, Along With Fan Yongkui, Were Taken Into Custody for Questioning

At around 10:00 PM the night before last, in a certain wine and vegetable restaurant at No. 600 Peng Road, just as it was about to close, two men speaking with a Chongming accent suddenly came to buy drinks and ordered the owner, Wen Jue-ting, to prepare exquisite wine and food for them to enjoy. The owner, thinking that customers were good for business, ordered the staff to do their best to entertain them. The two men sat at the table and ate heartily until around 11:00 PM, when the restaurant, having passed closing time, ordered the staff to close and advised the two men to stop drinking. At that time, the two men stopped drinking and asked the restaurant to settle the bill. Just then, one of the men suddenly said that he had forgotten to bring money, and the other man immediately said that he would go to a friend's place to borrow it, and then hurried out, telling his companion to wait for him in the restaurant. Unexpectedly, this man was gone for a long time and did not return. The restaurant, having no other choice, intended to hold the man's hat as collateral. In the midst of their dispute, Mr. Xu, a tenant from the floor above, heard the noise and came downstairs to investigate. He suddenly saw what appeared to be a weapon in the customer's sleeve, fearing that it would be harmful to the owner, so he grabbed the man from behind and snatched the object from his sleeve. Upon closer inspection, it turned out to be a fake handgun made of wood, looking very realistic. In the midst of the commotion, the owner's wife, Wen Li, returned from outside and saw another man outside the restaurant door, peeking in with a suspicious look. She quickly told the staff to run out and grab him, and then called the police to take them to the police station. Under questioning by the chief of police, they confessed that their names were Xue Qianglang and Tang Yingen, and that the fake handgun was given to them by a man named Fan Yongkui, hoping to do something illegal. After confirming Fan's address, detectives were dispatched to arrest Fan Yongkui, and together they were sent to court yesterday morning for further investigation.

Shen Xiaolin Buys People and Forces Them into Prostitution 136

Zhong Yuedou Escapes from the Fire Pit

Zhong Yuebao, a young woman from Pinghu, now 24 years old, was tricked into coming to Shanghai by her husband, Yan Changfa, in the spring of 1931. For the price of 260 yuan, Yuebao was sold to Shen Xiaolin's family as a goddaughter, ostensibly to learn opera, but in reality, she was forced to engage in prostitution. Even in severe cold or heat, and even when sick, she had to walk the streets. If no patrons stayed overnight, she would be whipped by Shen Xiaolin. For years, Yuebao suffered unbearably. Last month, she seized an opportunity to escape from the fire pit, renting a house to the left of Fangban Bridge and working to support herself. Recently, Shen Xiaolin discovered this and sued Zhong Yuebao in the District Court Prosecutor's Office for absconding with property. After questioning, the prosecutor charged Shen Xiaolin with obstructing morality. Yesterday morning, Judge Lu Hongyi opened the court session. First, Zhong Yuebao testified about the previous situation, stating that every year, as soon as the lights came on, she had to run to various hotels, such as the Ping An, Jiang Tai, and An Le on Zhu Bao San Road, and the Dongfang Yuebin Hotel at Xiaodongmen. During the day, she had to run to Yong An, Sincere, and New World department stores. "This time, I couldn't bear the hardship anymore. Even when I had a venereal sore on my body, I was still forced to receive customers. So, on the fifth day of the eleventh month, I ran away." Next, the witness Li Chunshan testified that he was a tailor from Hubei working at the Ping An Hotel. "She (referring to Zhong Yuebao) has been running to the hotels since the Shanghai war started, so I know her." Finally, Shen Xiaolin testified, "When Zhong Yuebao first came to my house, she already had a venereal disease. It's true that she ran to the hotels and made business deals, but she only did it for two months and sold imported goods, so she deserves the punishment." The judge ordered him to be released on bail with a 500 yuan written guarantee, and without bail, he was to be detained. The judgment was scheduled for the 31st. Zhong Yuebao was dismissed from the court.

Xu Qizhong Borrows Money and Turns It into a Criminal Case 137

Lawyer's Testimony Corroborates with Plaintiff

Defendant Claims to Have Copied the IOU and Signed the Check

Xu Qizhong, son of Xu Guannan, resident of No. 61 North Zhejiang Road, borrowed 40,000 yuan from Wang Bingzhong (also known as Zhu Ping Song), a Portuguese national, on May 22nd of this year, using three land title deeds as collateral. Later, Wang discovered that the land title deeds were forged, so he negotiated with Xu. However, Xu, due to his weak intellect, fled to Hangzhou in a panic. Wang then posted a reward and issued a wanted notice in the newspaper. The Hangzhou Public Security Bureau located Xu and notified the Chengdu Road Police Station, which sent Detective Yang Xinzheng to Hangzhou to bring Xu Qizhong back to Shanghai. The police charged Xu with fraud under Article 339 of the Criminal Law and forgery of documents under Article 210. The Special Court had already interrogated him once and ordered the defendant to post 40,000 yuan bail pending trial. This has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Liu Yugui continued the trial of this case in the Eighth Criminal Court. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated that during the adjournment, the police received an official letter from the court to investigate the Shanghai Bank on Rue Lafayette. According to manager Pan Bu-hou, who provided the account records, on May 22nd, the victim, Wang Bingzhong, had a deposit of 4,805.36 yuan. On the morning of the 23rd, another 2,900 yuan was deposited, bringing the total to 7,705.36 yuan. However, someone soon used check No. 313483 to withdraw 5,000 yuan. Later, Wang deposited 40,000 yuan in the bank on the same day, in eight installments of 5,000 yuan each. At the same time, someone also withdrew 40,000 yuan in eight installments, so Wang's deposit remained at 7,000 yuan when the accounts were settled at the end of the day. Judge Liu then ordered the witnesses to withdraw and be questioned separately. According to Wang Bingzhong's testimony, on May 23rd, he had a total deposit of over 47,000 yuan in the Shanghai Bank, and he presented the bank statement. "On May 22nd of this year, the defendant, Xu Qizhong, came to my office in Fuming Village, Rue Foochow, to borrow money, and insisted on my help. Because I knew Xu, I couldn't refuse, so I agreed. The guarantors on the IOU, Shen Shouheng, lawyers Shen Yiqian and Shen Boxiong, were all called by the defendant by telephone. The defendant personally wrote the IOU and handed over three land title deeds. Then I handed over eight checks, each for 5,000 yuan. This method was entirely proposed by the defendant. There was no stamp on the back of the check at that time. It was only later, when I retrieved the check from the bank, that I found the defendant's signature and stamp. When the IOU was signed, I was sitting facing south upstairs, lawyer Shen Yiqian was sitting facing north, the defendant was on my left, and Shen Shouheng and Shen Boxiong were walking back and forth in the room." The witnesses Shen Shouheng and lawyer Shen Yiqian successively testified about the situation at that time, and their statements were completely consistent with Wang Bingzhong's. Shen Yiqian even presented the defendant's handwritten power of attorney as evidence. When questioned, the defendant, Xu Qizhong, claimed, "The draft of the IOU has a bottom copy. He told me to copy the bill. The eight checks were also taken out by Wang, asking me to sign and stamp, and then he took them back. Wang gave me a bearer check for over 7,000 yuan to draw money. I went to the bank to withdraw the money myself!" The judge believed that the case still needed investigation and ordered a postponement to the 31st of this month for further trial. The defendant remained on the original bail.

We will continue to report later. Respectfully, The Head of the Chinese Buddhist Siamese Study Abroad Group, Shi Beiguan, and all members."

Round Trip Car Fare in the City Center Area 147

Xiang Sheng Company Complies with Regulations

One Dollar for a Single Trip

The Municipal Council, in order to facilitate citizens' travel to the city center area, had consulted with relevant bureaus and agreed on a uniform car fare. The regulations stipulate that, except for the Caohejing area, for trips to and from the city center area from districts like Hu Nan and Zhabei, as well as the two Special Districts, without any stops in between, the fare is one dollar per single trip. Last month, Xiang Sheng Company submitted a request to the bureau, agreeing to abide by the above regulations. They established a branch on Guohe Road in the city center area. However, the company subsequently published a statement, stipulating that the one-dollar fare for the city center area was still limited to twenty minutes, which was clearly inconsistent with the bureau's agreed-upon regulations. The bureau immediately ordered the company to correct the statement and report back. It is now learned that the company has responded, clarifying that the one-dollar fare for a single trip in the city center area has no twenty-minute time limit.

Kuai Huo Lin Film Company - Case of Defaming Qing Xin Girls' High School 148

Both Agents Claim Reconciliation is Still in Progress

Court Reschedules Hearing to January 4th of Next Year

Qing Xin Girls' High School, located in the Nanshi area of this city, on Lujiabang, was founded by the Presbyterian Church and has a history of seventy-five years. It is a famous girls' school in Shanghai. The school's facilities and operations are in accordance with the educational principles of the Republic of China and the decrees issued by the Ministry of Education. In the 18th year of the Republic [1929], it was approved for registration by the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau and has received repeated commendations. It enjoys a deep social trust, and the school's affairs are flourishing, with over nine hundred students. The school's management is very strict. All students must wear uniforms, and even on holidays, students are not allowed to go out without a significant reason, even if parents request leave. This is to instill discipline and prevent them from being contaminated by the bad habits of society. Recently, the Kuai Huo Lin Film Company's film "Little Aunt," starring actress Xia Peizhen, contained photographs and text involving Qing Xin Girls' High School. After Ms. Zhang Rongzhen, the current principal of Qing Xin Girls' High School, learned of this and went to see the film, she believed that the drama portrayed in the film deliberately defamed Qing Xin Girls' High School. Principal Zhang, in her capacity as the legal representative of Qing Xin Girls' High School, entrusted lawyer Zhou Yingcai to file a complaint with the Criminal Division of the Second Special District Court, accusing Zhang Bingsheng, the manager of Kuai Huo Lin Film Company, and Min Qian, the screenwriter and director, of deliberately spreading words and pictures to defame the school, requesting legal investigation in accordance with Article 310, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code. According to the indictment, in this year's film "Little Aunt," produced by Kuai Huo Lin Film Company, the plot involves a female student named Chen Lianzhen, who undergoes a sudden change in attitude after entering Qing Xin Girls' High School. She becomes fond of wearing fancy clothes, climbs over the school wall, enters and exits dance halls at will, and commits adultery with her sister's husband, named Yan Shaohua, disrupting her sister's family. Most hatefully, the film prominently features the school's large plaque with the six characters "Qing Xin Girls' High School," displayed in major theaters, making it clear to the audience that the events take place in the plaintiff's school. After being informed, the plaintiff went to see the film at the Southeast Grand Theater in the French Concession and immediately instructed a lawyer to send a warning letter. The defendants ignored it, thus deliberately defaming the school, requesting investigation and, furthermore, seeking civil compensation, demanding that the defendants compensate for losses, destroy the "Little Aunt" film, and publish apologies and corrections in major newspapers to avoid misunderstandings. The court approved the request and had Judge Sun Pengham summon the defendants for a hearing. Only Zhang Bingsheng, one of the defendants, sent a lawyer to represent him. As both parties agreed to reconciliation, the hearing was postponed. Yesterday morning, the hearing was to be resumed, but Ms. Zhang Rongzhen, the principal of Qing Xin Girls' High School, the plaintiff, was represented by a lawyer, who stated that the plaintiff was unable to attend due to school matters. Zhang Bingsheng, the defendant, was also represented by a lawyer, who stated that Zhang Bingsheng was unable to attend due to illness. The whereabouts of the second defendant, Min Qian, are unknown. Although the summons was received by the first defendant, it could not be delivered. Both lawyers stated that the case was currently under reconciliation and had not yet been resolved, requesting a one-week postponement to resolve the matter. The court agreed and postponed the hearing to January 4th of the 25th year, instructing both lawyers that if reconciliation is achieved outside of court, they should promptly submit a request to withdraw the complaint. Both lawyers complied and withdrew.

Municipal Council Schools - Prospects for Promoting Graduates' Employment are Promising 150

Excellent Students to be Registered

At a recent meeting of the Municipal Council's Education Committee, the Health Department suggested that outstanding graduates from the Municipal Council's schools should be employed as trainees or clerks by various departments of the Municipal Council, to broaden students' employment prospects. According to the department's report, there are currently four vacancies for trainees, with an age requirement of around twenty-one. It is preferred that they have been out of school for some time and have some understanding of the world. The deputy director of the department stated that most of the trainees currently employed by the department come from the Municipal Council's schools. The current practice is that when the department has vacancies, the Education Committee informs the school authorities or student associations, who then select students with exceptional character and academic performance to be trainees. However, there is no explicit regulation, so the deputy director strongly desires that the Municipal Council establish regulations for outstanding graduates of the Municipal Council's schools to broaden their employment prospects. The director of the Education Department also stated that other departments of the Municipal Council are adopting this method, such as the Police Department, which employs Chinese trainees and gradually promotes them to the position of Chinese Deputy Inspector. A committee member immediately stated that the employment of graduates from Municipal Council schools should not be limited to the Health Department and the Police Department. Other departments should also consider employing them, and it should not be limited to male students. Female students should also have equal opportunities, and it should not be limited to Chinese youth. Westerners should also be treated equally. Thus, this issue involves the provision of vocational education. However, the Municipal Council is limited in its economic resources for vocational education, and the issues are complex, making it difficult to address all aspects at once. For example, home economics classes for girls' schools have not yet been established. After discussion, it was decided that the director of the Education Department should propose regulations on how to register students from Municipal Council schools who achieve certain scores in their graduation examinations, to give them priority for employment by the Municipal Council in the future. It is reported that the above regulations proposed by the Education Committee have been approved by the Municipal Council's board of directors.

Minimum Shipping Quantity for Acetic Acid, etc. 151

Ministry of Railways Approves Ninety Kilograms

Effective January 21st of Next Year

The Ministry of Railways instructed the two Railway Bureaus, stating that the United Federation of the National Chinese Medicine Industry Association had submitted a request to revise the regulations for the transportation of pharmaceuticals such as acetic acid, carbolic acid, and liquid ammonia. After investigation, acetic acid, carbolic acid, and liquid ammonia are essential pharmaceutical products. To maintain the medical supply, the Ministry approves adding the above three pharmaceuticals to the list of dangerous goods with a minimum shipping quantity of fifty kilograms, effective January 21st of the 25th year. However, to prevent accidents, the packaging methods for the above pharmaceuticals should be communicated to the pharmaceutical merchants. All shipments must be packed in wooden crates filled with wood shavings. However, the item "Ammonia Water" listed in the appendix of the 10th order of the Ye Zi Department from January 10th of the 23rd year should be removed. In addition to the instructions, you are instructed to comply and report back." The bureau has instructed the Transportation Department to comply and report back.

Another Municipal Council Tax Dispute 156

Lawyer Huang Renlong Unwilling to Pay Taxes

Lawyer Huang Renlong previously leased premises from the Shanghai Bank at the intersection of Qipu Road, opposite the First Special District Court on North Zhejiang Road, to establish a law firm. At the end of September of this year, due to the relocation of the law firm, he terminated the lease agreement with the landlord. However, the Municipal Council's Tax Office has recently continued to collect the property tax for the summer, autumn, and winter quarters of this year. Huang argued that since he had vacated the premises on October 1st, he should not be responsible for the tax for October, November, and December. He refused to pay. The Municipal Council subsequently filed a petition with the Civil Mediation Office of the First Special District Local Court, requesting Huang to appear in court for mediation. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Meng Tingke opened the court. Huang Renlong presented the court's judgment on the termination of the lease agreement with the landlord, proving that he had indeed vacated the premises on October 1st. He also stated that someone else was responsible for the tax for the summer and autumn quarters and that he could not be collected from him. The representative of the Municipal Council's Tax Office stated that the outstanding tax should be paid by Huang. As mediation failed, Judge Meng ordered both parties to withdraw and instructed the plaintiff to file a formal lawsuit for hearing.

Old Deeds Mortgaged for Certificate Registration 158

Deadline of Three Months, No Longer Accepted After Deadline

Mortgages with old deeds have long been a common practice in Shanghai. However, many people still do not apply to the Land Bureau for certificate exchange and registration. Once a dispute arises, requests are often submitted to the bureau to prevent the issuance of certificates, etc. The bureau generally rejects these requests because the proper procedures have not been followed. As there are still many old deeds mortgaged and held by the people, it seems appropriate to give them the opportunity to exchange and register their certificates. Director Cai of the Land Bureau has set a deadline and issued a public notice to the people of the city. The public notice is reproduced below: "After the Land Bureau has surveyed and issued land ownership certificates in the surveyed areas of the city, all transfers and mortgages by owners have been subject to the rules and procedures established by the bureau. In areas that have not been surveyed, the sale of old deeds has also been subject to established procedures. However, there are still many old deeds mortgaged and held by the people. The people are accustomed to complacency or are mutually constrained, and they often do not apply for certificate exchange. Once a dispute arises, requests are often submitted to the bureau to prevent the issuance of certificates and transfers. Since these mortgages with old deeds do not comply with the regulations for certificate exchange and registration with the bureau, it seems that they should not be subject to stop issuance and transfer orders. However, it is not appropriate to not give the opportunity to exchange and register existing land deeds for mortgages. The bureau has decided to set a deadline of three months. Regardless of whether the land has been surveyed or not, if there are any mortgages with old deeds, the mortgagee and mortgagor must come to the bureau together to exchange certificates or survey and exchange certificates, and at the same time apply for land certificate mortgage registration. If disputes arise after the deadline, and requests are submitted to the bureau to stop the issuance and transfer of certificates, they will not be accepted. As for those who have previously submitted disputes over mortgages to the bureau, they will be temporarily allowed to stop the issuance and transfer of certificates, but they must still pay the land mortgage registration fee according to the fee schedule (it must be noted in the registration that the issuance and transfer of certificates are stopped, which is called signing and registering). In this way, mortgages with old deeds can be cleared up and certificates exchanged as soon as possible. The above measures have been submitted to the municipal government for approval. A public notice is hereby issued to the people of the city, so that all landowners with old deeds mortgaged should comply with the above deadline and come to the bureau to exchange certificates without further delay. The notice is hereby issued. December 28th, 24th year of the Republic of China. Cai Zengji, Director of the Land Bureau (acting)."

Jiaxu Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association - Scheduled to End Entirely at the End of This Month 162

Work Relief Has Completed Thirteen Counties

Currently Editing the Final Report

The Jiaxu Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association in Shanghai has decided to conclude operations at the end of this month, as work relief in various locations has mostly been completed. The association sent letters to various county governments yesterday, urging them to fill out and submit various forms to the association, and is actively compiling the final report. The details gathered by the reporter are as follows:

Work Relief Situation - To ensure that the relief funds are not wasted, the association has organized work relief projects in addition to providing various forms of relief. Plans were prepared, and work relief directors were assigned to various counties to dredge waterways and build roads. All able-bodied men receiving relief food were required to participate in the work. Since its inception, it has been nearly a year. Currently, Jiaxing, Haiyan, Chongde, Tongxiang, Haining, Yuhang, Wukang, Deqing, Shangyu, Xinchang, Shengxian, Shaoxing, Yuyao, and thirteen other counties have completed their projects in sequence. The county directors have also reported to the association. Only Shangyu County's dredging of small rivers and irrigation of farmland with water from the Cao'e River have not been fully completed. Work is actively underway and is expected to be fully completed by the end of January next year.

Conclusion of Operations - As relief efforts in Zhejiang Province have gradually become more effective and work relief has also been completed, the association has decided to conclude operations entirely at the end of this year. Yesterday, letters were sent to the county governments of Tonglu, Jiande, Zhuji, Fuyang, Hangzhou County, Dongyang, and other counties regarding the conclusion of operations. The letter urged the counties to fill out and submit the actual quantity of relief grain used to compile a report for submission to the central government. At the same time, to show the results of the relief efforts to the public, the association will compile a report on the income from donations, various expenditure items, and the progress of relief work, and distribute it to various sectors. The draft is currently being prepared and will be sent to print soon. It is expected to be published and distributed in mid-next month.

The Shanghai Public Security Bureau released statistics yesterday on the criminal cases that occurred within the city limits during the past week, from December 21st to December 27th of the 24th year [of the Republic]. A total of 230 cases were reported, and a total of 296 suspects, male and female, were apprehended. The details are as follows: Robbery and aggravated robbery: 12 cases, 21 suspects; Theft: 82 cases, 133 suspects; Assault: 20 cases, 24 suspects; Kidnapping and abduction: 24 cases, 44 suspects; Heroin and morphine: 12 cases, 10 suspects; Gambling: 4 cases, 18 suspects; Fraud: 17 cases, 26 suspects; Conspiracy: 1 case, 3 suspects; Counterfeiting: 4 cases, 4 suspects; Violation of police regulations: 4 cases, 13 suspects; Other criminal cases: 48 cases, 70 suspects. Total: 230 cases, 296 suspects. After preliminary examination by the Third Section, all apprehended suspects have been handed over to the local court or other competent authorities for trial, except for 84 cases that were minor and handled according to police regulations or sentenced to fines. The number of reported criminal cases decreased by 6 compared to the previous week, and the number of apprehended suspects decreased by 76.

Cypress Wax Trade Association General Meeting 171

The Shanghai Cypress Wax Trade Association held a general meeting the day before yesterday (the 26th) at 2:00 PM. More than ten representatives attended, including Fan Zonglin, Ye Quanbo (representing Ye Guangjiu), Wu Junzhi, Wang Zhihong, and Shi Runsheng (representing Fan Zonglin). Wang Zhihong presided over the meeting, and Chen Guanzhou served as the recorder. First, Mr. Wang reported that the industry had adopted the use of the market kilogram on March 15, 1933, and on May 19 of the same year, the Bureau of Social Affairs issued Order No. 2260, instructing (to order all industry firms, those who have changed to new instruments, must not reuse old instruments, or new and old ones together), etc. Having been issued, letters have already been sent to all members. Fearing that it would be ignored over time, it was resolved on November 19 of this year (the old (scales) (guild) that the members prepared, whether purchased at their own expense or at public expense, will all be taken back by the guild and cut off), and a letter was sent to all members. According to the guild's report, most of the old instruments have been recovered, but a certain company is making excuses for not handing them over. How should it be handled? Should the selling price be changed? Please make a decision. It was resolved that the old instruments of the company that made excuses for not handing them over are indeed violating the law. For the sake of the industry, please ask Mr. Zhang to go and persuade them to hand them over. The price of tallow oil remains the same: white wax is uniformly 125 yuan, and rice wicks are reduced by 5 yuan.

Yuyao Lao's Traumatology Practice Opens in Shanghai 174

The Lao family of traumatologists in Zhouxiang, Yuyao, has been practicing medicine since ancient times, and has saved countless lives. Within 200 li of their hometown, everyone knows of their divine skills. In recent years, people from eastern Zhejiang living in Shanghai, either individuals or factories, have suddenly been injured, and special messengers have often been sent to Shanghai to invite them for diagnosis. After Lao returned to Yuyao after medical treatment, before they had a chance to rest, those who requested their services in Shanghai arrived again, causing them much hardship. Mr. Lao Qi'an and others agreed, and have already established a residence at No. 10 Renxing Lane, Route des Peres (east end of Route Saopaze) in the French Concession. Publishing World 181

The 8th Issue of "Chinese Postal Worker" Published. The Chinese Postal Worker Monthly, published by the Propaganda Department of the National Postal Workers' Union of China in Shanghai, has rich content and thorough arguments, and is a great contribution of postal workers nationwide to the cultural world. Therefore, since its publication, it has been popular throughout the country. Currently, it is heard that there are more than 30,000 subscribers, making it the publication with the widest circulation in the country. Now, the first volume, eighth issue of the publication has been published, and the content is even more rich. In addition to four short and concise current event commentaries, there are articles by Zhang Naiqi on "The Significance and Prospects of Monetary Reform," Jingguan on "My Views on the Theory and Implementation of the Establishment of the Chinese Postal Worker Correspondence School," Xiao Weng on "The Morbid Outlook of Modern Youth," and Youxing on "Two Major Overseas Territories on China's Border." The arguments are all very insightful. There is a translation by Zuo Qi of "A Brief History of the Labor Movement in Various Countries of the World," which is a continuous translation and a systematic reference material for studying the history of the labor movement in various countries. The Social Survey section includes "Memoirs of the Disaster of the Yunnan Post Office" and "Survey of the Tianjin Yarn Industry," both of which are reports of field investigations. The Art and Literature section includes humorous essays, selections of new and old poems, and original novels. There is a "Postal Knowledge" column in the publication, which provides detailed and systematic descriptions of postal services and various procedures. People outside the industry who do not fully understand postal procedures or want to study postal science can use it as a good reference. Other sections, such as Postal News and the Appendix, also publish various postal regulations that are not easily accessible to the outside world. The "Chronicle of Major Events of Domestic and Foreign Workers" is an important reference material for those studying labor issues.

Chinese Basketball Court Packed to the Brim Lianghua Loses to Pirates Yesterday 185

31 to 35 A Big Disappointment for Fans

Lianghua, Three Wins and One Loss, Returns North Tomorrow

Lianghua vs. Pirates, last night at the Shenyuan basketball court as a final game before leaving Shanghai, that is, the final competition with the Pirates. People in Shanghai, admiring the deep skills of the two teams, although in the midst of this rainy weather, gathered in groups, heading to the secluded Yanping Road. The basketball court was filled with more than 3,000 people, almost making it difficult to breathe, a truly unprecedented grand occasion.

Three Thousand Fans

The reason why this game attracted such great attention is that the Pirates have been dominating Shanghai for five years, and I don't know how many times the Chinese teams in Shanghai have been ravaged by them. Lianghua's five tigers defeated them with a score of 50 to 43 the night before, avenging two years of resentment. Therefore, everyone wanted to witness the event and find out what happened. Moreover, the tickets were only sold for half a yuan, a low price, which contributed to the turnout. Even reporters from various newspapers were barred from entering the venue.

Forced to Start

It was learned that the tickets for last night were purchased as early as 4:00 PM, and were sold out by 6:00 PM. The venue was already packed to the brim. The audience, blocked outside the bamboo fence, gathered more and more, and even rushed in, making it impossible to maintain order. When the game was about to start, the audience was standing more than two feet past the boundary line. In this cramped situation, the game was forced to start.

Heroes Nod

It is heard that the Lianghua team will return to the north tomorrow. This time they came to Shanghai again, and fought four fierce battles with Chinese and Western powerhouses. They first defeated McLeans, then defeated Jinan, and then defeated the Pirates. Yesterday they were defeated by the Pirates, with three wins and one loss, a brilliant record. The Association specially presented a silver cup with the inscription "Heroes Nod" to commemorate the occasion.

Being Inferior

Lianghua and Pirates played their second game at the Shenyuan basketball court last night. The game was not able to start until 8:00 PM. The two armies started contact in a crowd, and the Pirates won the opening victory. They led all the way and always occupied the first place. Although Lianghua tried hard to catch up, they finally lost with a score of 11 to 19 in the first half. The 3,000 fans, in high spirits, all felt unhappy. In the second half, Lianghua vowed not to give in, and worked hard to improve. The closest they got was 33 to 30, only three points apart. But in the end, they still lost with a score of 35 to 31. Economic Difficulties: Students Returning from Japan En Masse 196

Tickets for Connecting Ships Booked Through February of Next Year

In recent years, the number of Chinese students studying in Japan has increased due to the low exchange rate of the Japanese yen and the reduced cost of living. Elementary School Students' Science Speech Contest: Finals Today 201

Starting at 1:00 PM at Shangwen Elementary School

Twenty-Two Students Were Selected from Yesterday's Preliminaries

The Science Speech Contest for Elementary School Students, organized by the Municipal Education Bureau, was held yesterday afternoon starting at 1:00 PM at Shangwen Elementary School. A total of eighty-four students participated, divided into three groups for the preliminary rounds. Twenty-two students were selected to advance to the finals, which will be held today at 1:00 PM, also at Shangwen Elementary School. Details are as follows:

Opening Ceremony

The opening ceremony was held at 1:00 PM in the auditorium of Shangwen Elementary School. The chair was the section chief of the association, the master of ceremonies was Qian Fugong, and the recorder was Wu Renya. Following customary procedures, the chair gave a report, briefly stating that the Education Bureau was organizing the Science Speech Contest for Elementary School Students in accordance with the Ministry's directives, to promote scientific knowledge, encourage students' interest in scientific research, and improve their public speaking skills. He stated that the world is now a world of science, and a country's strength depends on the development of science, while a country's decline depends on the backwardness of science. Therefore, the popularization of scientific knowledge is particularly important in China. A total of eighty-four participants competed, divided into three groups, with seven students selected from each group to advance to tomorrow's finals. The competition then commenced immediately.

Preliminary Rounds

The competition was divided into three preliminary rounds. The first group included students numbered 1 to 28, with judges Xie Engao, Hu Shuyi, Hua Li, and timekeeper Wang Gongxia. The second group included students numbered 29 to 56, with judges Yao Zantang, Zhang Yongchun, Li Kun, and timekeeper Shi Chongpeng. The third group included students numbered 57 to 84, with judges Jiang Wenbao, Tang Mingbai, and Lü Hailan, and timekeeper Luo Zhongyu. The speeches concluded at 4:30 PM.

Preliminary Results

Hui Shengdian reported the results of the preliminary rounds. With the exception of the first group, where eight students were selected due to a tie between two students, seven students were selected from each group. The list of names is as follows: First Group: Chen Wenhan (No. 22, Zhongzhen), Zhou Zilong (No. 28, Wanzhu), Zai Jiawei (No. 1, Fahua), Liu Zilin (No. 19, Minzhi), Liang Dong (No. 16, Xinmin), Ge Qizhen (No. 5, Huiqun), Shen Yanlong (No. 23, Kunfan), Deng Lanpei (No. 20, Hubei). Guan Cheng Huan's total score was 80.3, winning the third prize.

The Municipal Public Knowledge Guidance Committee will hold its third broadcast lecture on January 6th at 3:45 PM at the Great China Radio Station. Ms. Cai Jinying, a standing director of the Municipal Women's Association and a teacher at Wuben Women's Middle School, will lecture on the rational life of women.

The Chinese Personnel Management Association held its second anti-corruption discussion meeting yesterday, chaired by Pan Yangyao. It was resolved to implement anti-corruption measures, divided into fundamental and symptomatic approaches.

Children's Educational Novel: Little Men (1)(3)(8) 204

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

At this point, Rob appeared again, cautiously bringing what Asey called a "small biscuit," meaning baked in the shape of a small dish.

"The filling in this has some of the blackberries that I picked. I'll give you half at dinner," he announced proudly and solemnly.

Nanen gently asked, "What made you think of treating me so well when I was so naughty?"

"Because we got lost together. You won't be naughty again, will you?"

"Never," Nanen said, speaking with great determination.

"Oh, good! Now I'm going to Amelie to have her cut it up for us so we can eat it; it's almost dinner time," Rob said, waving the little sweet biscuit to encourage her to come with him.

Nanen was about to go with him when she suddenly stopped and said:

"I forgot, I can't go."

"Just try," Mrs. Pei said, seeing that she had secretly untied the rope while she was talking to Rob.

Seeing that she was free again, Nanen eagerly kissed Mrs. Shu, and then rushed away, as swift as a bird, followed by Rob, as the berry juice dripped from his hand along the way.

Wartime Education Work Plan (4) Colleagues of the Education Research Institute of Sun Yat-sen University 205

3. High School Wartime Work Plan

A. Organizational System

The wartime work organization of high schools is based on the original military training and first aid organizations.

The organizational system takes the school's wartime work committee as the highest authority, the team as the central organization, and the group as the basic organization.

Groups are divided according to the nature of the work, such as first aid groups and fire-fighting groups. Each group has about ten people, regardless of class.

If there are several groups for one type of work, they are called "Group Number X of So-and-So" (such as the Firefighting Group), and there is a joint group meeting for communication and progress.

Each student should join a group according to their abilities and interests, and each group elects one representative.

Three or four groups form a team.

Each team has a captain and vice-captain, appointed by the principal from teachers and students.

Teachers are natural consultants for each group.

Staff and workers are free to participate in the work of a certain group.

The school's wartime work committee has five departments: (1) Personnel Registration, (2) Needs Investigation, (3) Skills Training, (4) Academic Guidance, and (5) Social Work.

Each country is both a component of the team and subject to the jurisdiction of the corresponding department of the school committee in order to ensure the consistency of the school's work.

The organizational chart of each level of group is as follows:

B. Work Outline

Distribute questionnaires to investigate each person's abilities and interests.

Categorize and register various wartime personnel.

Dispatch students to designated areas to investigate the needs in various aspects of wartime.

Change the original teaching time of each subject, extracting twelve hours per week to teach new wartime teaching materials. The distribution method for the extracted time is as follows:

(1) Entirely extracted

(2) Extracted by half

(3) No time extracted, Suan Wei (arithmetic), ethics.

Supplement the new wartime teaching materials compiled by the provincial wartime work committee according to local conditions.

The teaching of new wartime teaching materials is the responsibility of the original teachers of each subject, but local experts may also be invited to serve as instructors.

Disseminate wartime news at any time.

Practical work should especially focus on the training of several technologies.

In addition to general work, practical work focuses on the following items, which are undertaken by groups. Each week, a total of six hours of training is conducted.

1. Writing news articles and oral propaganda. 2. Intensifying military training. 3. Female student first aid training. 4. Making gas masks. 5. Making fire extinguishers. 6. Investigating the required quantity of daily necessities. 7. Investigating and manufacturing military supplies. 8. Digging cellars. 9. Building roads, directing vehicles. 10. Connecting military electrical lines. 11. Maintaining public order. 12. Teaching the public.

The principal supervises and inspects the work situation at any time, and the local wartime work committee sends personnel to inspect on a regular basis.

In addition to government funding, the funds required for wartime work training are freely donated by staff and students.

C. Implementation Steps

The principal convenes an emergency wartime meeting to discuss wartime work preparations. The members of the school's wartime work committee take an oath. Teachers go to the local wartime work committee for training. Investigate the abilities and wishes of all staff, students, workers, and staff. Announce the names of the members of each group. Each group elects a representative. Form the middle team. The school committee investigates wartime needs and informs each team to be responsible for meeting them separately. Hold team meetings to formulate a work plan. Raise funds to purchase equipment. Implement training. Start work.

Yesterday's 15th Anniversary of Liangjiang 206

Difficult National Situation, Therefore No Celebration

Set Goals and Work Earnestly

The Liangjiang Women's Physical Education School in Jiangwan, Shanghai, was founded 15 years ago. After several setbacks, Principal Lu Lihua is determined to promote women's physical education and cultivate talents. After working hard, the school is becoming more and more prosperous. The current site covers nearly 50 acres, and the school buildings are gradually being built. The environment is quiet, which is especially a good place for reading and writing. Yesterday was the 15th anniversary of the school's founding. Due to the difficult national situation, there was no celebration. At 9:00 AM, all the teachers and students held a simple memorial ceremony in the auditorium. Principal Lu gave a moving report on the difficult struggles of the past ten years and expressed great hope for future progress. According to the school's first-step reconstruction plan after the January 28th Incident, the plan has been achieved. Its second-step plan, such as building a gymnasium, library, and general office building, is being planned. School directors, faculty, staff, students, and alumni are actively working together for the future of the school, hoping to achieve the entire realization in the near future. Buried in hard work, earnestly carry out, which is helpful to the development of women's physical education prospects, is very significant.
